  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1f63870d-b8d2-4a43-87f8-584810cb0e98'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer8679917566674645920">The <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of <i>Spandau Phoenix</i> and <i>Mortal Fear</i> returns with a rich and atmospheric novel of high suspense<br/><br/>When recently widowed Penn Cage leaves Houston with his young daughter and returns to his hometown seeking peace, he finds something very different. Natchez, Mississippi, is the jewel of the antebellum South, a city of old secrets and older mon</span>
  <span id="freeText8679917566674645920" style="display:none">The <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of <i>Spandau Phoenix</i> and <i>Mortal Fear</i> returns with a rich and atmospheric novel of high suspense<br /><br />When recently widowed Penn Cage leaves Houston with his young daughter and returns to his hometown seeking peace, he finds something very different. Natchez, Mississippi, is the jewel of the antebellum South, a city of old secrets and older money. Upon learning that his father is being blackmailed, Penn finds himself reopening the most highly charged murder case in the town's history, searching for the evidence that could bring down the judge who nearly destroyed his father years ago. As the town closes ranks against him, Penn is joined by Caitlin Masters, a young newspaper publisher, on a deadly quest to find answers to one of the darkest chapters of American history, a quest that pits them against the FBI, a band of brothers still fiercely guarding the tainted legacy of J. Edgar Hoover. But Penn's most dangerous journey must be made alone--into the abiding mystery of his own past, into the mind and heart of a woman he lost twenty years ago, and who still has the power to save or destroy him.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8679917566674645920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1334889428" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1334889428" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1334889428?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/25910002-the-quiet-game">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Every-fucking-body with eyes</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1334889428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5576113730532873856"><b>WINNER: BEST THRILLER READ IN 2015!</b><br/><br/>Lemme tell you a story.<br/><br/>I'm perusing the stacks at my local Books-a-Million (hitherto referred to as BAM), when I come across an absolutely gorgeous hardcover by a guy named Greg Iles. That novel was <i>Natchez Burning</i>, and if you're ever at BAM or any other brick-and-mortar bookseller, check it out. Shoot, maybe you own this marvel of modern publishing. I wanna have babies with that hardcover. Papercuts on my dinglehopper be damned! Anyfuck, I'm wiping drool from </span>
  <span id="freeText5576113730532873856" style="display:none"><b>WINNER: BEST THRILLER READ IN 2015!</b><br /><br />Lemme tell you a story.<br /><br />I'm perusing the stacks at my local Books-a-Million (hitherto referred to as BAM), when I come across an absolutely gorgeous hardcover by a guy named Greg Iles. That novel was <i>Natchez Burning</i>, and if you're ever at BAM or any other brick-and-mortar bookseller, check it out. Shoot, maybe you own this marvel of modern publishing. I wanna have babies with that hardcover. Papercuts on my dinglehopper be damned! Anyfuck, I'm wiping drool from my mouth as I pull out my phone and bring up my Goodreads app. Fuck my couch and call me Naugahyde, <i>Natchez Burning</i> is the <i>FOURTH</i> goddamn book in a series starring author/lawyer Penn Cage. What's a book junkie to do? Start the series at the beginning, that's what.<br /><br />Horribly tragic side note: <i>The Bone Tree (Penn Cage #5)</i> just came out and it's just as fucking sexy as it's predecessor. My lights are gonna get cut off, people, but at least I'mma have some pretty books to read by candlelight.<br /><br />Back on track. After ogling <i>Natchez Burning</i>, I traipsed over to my second favorite stomping grounds (Trade N Books in Montgomery, AL) to find the first three Penn Cage books because BAM didn't have any of the earlier novels. Bad BAM! Shame on you! Luckily, my used bookseller had the first and the third books in the series. I bought them posthaste. This was two weeks ago. I went back today, after having finished the first novel last night, and they had the second book. Series acquired. Let the Greg Iles marathon begin!<br /><br /><i>The Quiet Game</i> is one of those novels that defies categorization. It is equal parts action, suspense, courtroom drama, and literary novel. There's even a bit of horror toward the end. (The last meeting with Ike Ransom was intense and disturbing. Two words: Bone fragments). And the final court case damn near gave me an anxiety attack. <br /><br />I know absolutely dick about lawyer-type shenanigans, but I understood everything in this book. Iles does a fantastic job of dropping knowledge on your ass without making it feel as if you're taking a law course at a community college. In other words, this novel is never boring. It grips you from the first page and hooks you through the bag until the end. I read the final 200 pages in a day. Couldn't put the book down. Iles ends every chapter in such a way that you feel the pressing urgency to continue on. And when you do put the book down you feel as if you've lost a friend. <br /><br />In summation: I could go on and on about the terrific twists and the brutality and the tragedy and the stellar dialogue but I won't. I will tell you to read it and find out for yourself. Now would you kindly fuck off so I can start the next book in the series. Peace!<br /><br /><b>Final Judgment: You'll break the bank searching for the rest of this guy's books.</b><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5576113730532873856" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <i>"Our actions have consequences that last long after us, entwining the present with the future in ways we cannot begin to understand." </i>
</b><br/>—Greg Iles, The Quiet Game<br/> <br/>Going into this book, I didn’t know what to expect. I read <i>Cemetery Road</i> last year and was nearly waterlogged by the time I'd finished. As far as I was concerned, this author had a mountain to climb, but Mr. Iles soon proved that it wasn’t even a hill for a high-stepper like him!<br/><br/>The main character, Penn Cage, is brilliantly fleshed o</span>
  <span id="freeText7379865844038619054" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"Our actions have consequences that last long after us, entwining the present with the future in ways we cannot begin to understand." </i>
</b><br />—Greg Iles, The Quiet Game<br /> <br />Going into this book, I didn’t know what to expect. I read <i>Cemetery Road</i> last year and was nearly waterlogged by the time I'd finished. As far as I was concerned, this author had a mountain to climb, but Mr. Iles soon proved that it wasn’t even a hill for a high-stepper like him!<br /><br />The main character, Penn Cage, is brilliantly fleshed out and I liked him from the outset. Surrounded by a great supporting cast, I was invested in the well-being of these people, with whom I got cozy as I settled into the fictional streets of Natchez, Mississippi.<br /> <br /><i>"We are always spiraling around something, whether we see it or not, a secret center of gravity with the invisible power of a black hole."</i><br /><br />Cage is the quintessential small-town-boy-done-well until tragedy strikes. He soon realizes he is metaphorically swimming against the current with one arm tied behind his back and is losing the fight. The young lawyer packs up his life in Houston and heads back home to Natchez to figure out his next steps. In this case, the saying ‘you can’t go home again’ should be changed to ‘going home again will kill you, boy!’ From the moment he steps onto a plane bound for Mississippi, fate throws a wrench into the works of every plan, changing the course of his life and those of everyone around him.<br /><br />Filled with explosions, gunplay, and some southern heat, <i>The Quiet Game</i> is anything but quiet.</span>

          </span>

        <a title="Carolyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn">Carolyn</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19483764-the-quiet-game">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=murder-mystery">murder-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2068892143" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15592212515374054916">Greg Iles sure knows how to pack a lot into one novel! Starting somewhat slowly with lawyer and author Penn Cage returning to his home town of Natchez where he discovers his father being blackmailed this moves into a full-on thriller about a supposedly unsolved 35 year old murder that was covered up. Initially thought to be racially motivated Penn soon discovers other motives involving power, greed, corruption and politics. It's a complex and action packed thriller that soon has the bodies mount</span>
  <span id="freeText15592212515374054916" style="display:none">Greg Iles sure knows how to pack a lot into one novel! Starting somewhat slowly with lawyer and author Penn Cage returning to his home town of Natchez where he discovers his father being blackmailed this moves into a full-on thriller about a supposedly unsolved 35 year old murder that was covered up. Initially thought to be racially motivated Penn soon discovers other motives involving power, greed, corruption and politics. It's a complex and action packed thriller that soon has the bodies mounting up as Penn strives to untangle the lies and deception to find the truth, aided by journalist Caitlin, risking his own life and that of his daughter and parents. <br /><br />It took me a little while to get into this book, and perhaps it is a little longer than needed, but Iles is a very good writer and spinner of tales and it was well worth sticking with it. I loved Penn's relationship and care for his little daughter Annie while they are both still grieving for Penn's wife after her death from cancer the previous year. I also enjoyed the courtroom scenes where Penn is up against his old high school sweetheart and lost love, Olivia Marston. The southern vibe of Natchez works well with old prejudices and loyalties affecting Penn and Caitlin's search for the truth. Recommended for those who like big thrillers with lots of action, multiple bodies and some well placed twists and turns.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15592212515374054916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9846168580327036587">My first book by this author and I am not quite sure how to rate it. <br/>Firstly it was far too long. I like long books but only when the length contributes to the narrative. This one was just padded and I did skim large parts of it.<br/>Then it had far too many and too violent deaths with apparently no repercussions.   <span id="freeText9846168580327036587" style="display:none">My first book by this author and I am not quite sure how to rate it. <br />Firstly it was far too long. I like long books but only when the length contributes to the narrative. This one was just padded and I did skim large parts of it.<br />Then it had far too many and too violent deaths with apparently no repercussions. At times it seemed every character was getting bumped off without a policeman in sight. Or if there was one he was corrupt. Unrealistic.<br />On the other hand I found Penn Cage a very likeable character and wanted to hear more about him. I felt that the author could have made a lot more of the court room scene and a bit less of being shot at and riding water rapids in an inflatable dinghy.<br />The story was good and there was plenty of excitement. It really just needed an editor with a red pen to reduce it to an appropriate length. Having been assured by someone whose reading choices I trust that Iles is an excellent author I will try another of his books.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer590305227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18236563736949157629">This is by far the best I have read from Iles so far. A very riveting tale full of lies, deceit, mistrust, and brutal honesty. The plot was brilliant, the characters even more so, so vivid that you could place yourself there among them. My favorite character would have to be Penn Cage. I can honestly say that I will not forget him for a very long time, if ever. I look forward to the other books in this series. I can only see Cage becoming even more amazing.<br/><br/>I loved the twists that Iles included i</span>
  <span id="freeText18236563736949157629" style="display:none">This is by far the best I have read from Iles so far. A very riveting tale full of lies, deceit, mistrust, and brutal honesty. The plot was brilliant, the characters even more so, so vivid that you could place yourself there among them. My favorite character would have to be Penn Cage. I can honestly say that I will not forget him for a very long time, if ever. I look forward to the other books in this series. I can only see Cage becoming even more amazing.<br /><br />I loved the twists that Iles included in this book. As soon as you recover from one, he gives you another to ponder over. The plot was so believable, that it got me thinking about how real it all could be. All the possible cover ups, conspiracy, FBI, the government at it's finest. Iles takes you back in time to life in the 60's in the deep South. And then brings you up to present day with a Prosecuting Attorney, turned Author, trying to right a 'very' wrong. Simply Awesome!<br /><br />It is a very fast paced, exciting read. I became so involved in this story I could not even dream of putting the book down. At first I thought it was gonna get way too political for me but that was not the case at all. So many surprises that keep you turning the pages. I loved every minute of it. This is definitely suspense at it's finest.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3232449336" />
    <a title="Victoria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22727329-victoria"><img alt="Victoria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467838647p2/22727329.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3232449336?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria" href="/user/show/22727329-victoria">Victoria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780525937937" href="/book/show/815439.The_Quiet_Game">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3232449336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12395564932973175408">After enjoying Iles’ standalone, Cemetery Road, I quickly put his Natchez trilogy on my shelves, but wanted to dive in even earlier, to the origins of Penn Cage and that’s this book, the <i>very</i> first in the Natchez saga and it did not disappoint.<br/><br/>Iles delivers that perfect combination of an absorbing plot, intriguing characters and writing that is intelligent without trying to impress. Having recently read an author whose overwrought prose drove me to distraction, I appreciate Iles’ writing and sto</span>
  <span id="freeText12395564932973175408" style="display:none">After enjoying Iles’ standalone, Cemetery Road, I quickly put his Natchez trilogy on my shelves, but wanted to dive in even earlier, to the origins of Penn Cage and that’s this book, the <i>very</i> first in the Natchez saga and it did not disappoint.<br /><br />Iles delivers that perfect combination of an absorbing plot, intriguing characters and writing that is intelligent without trying to impress. Having recently read an author whose overwrought prose drove me to distraction, I appreciate Iles’ writing and storytelling style all the more.<br /><br />This is a propulsive narrative with its origins tracing back to J. Edgar Hoover, an unsolved murder whose tentacles surround the town of Natchez, conspiracies abound, the trail of bodies stack up and all eventually lead to an unforgettable trial. It’s multi-layered and suspenseful, emotional and action packed, this latter a little over the top and my only quibble. I’d like to see a wee bit less testosterone in the next in the series, incredulity was stretched with what Cage endures.<br /><br />I read more books last year than any previous and yet enjoyed my reading life less. A combination of a lot of factors which I won’t bore you with, but that has led me to a different approach, one of which is to include more of the authors I’ve enjoyed in the past, even if it’s not the current ‘must read.’ The Quiet Game paid off dividends on my new reading strategy and reading investment and I’m looking forward to more. 4+++</span>
  <a data-text-id="12395564932973175408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6086392058412014592" style="display:none">This was an excellent read, with interesting characters and plot, and sustained tension.<br /><br />It also provides a look at the ugly prejudice against blacks that apparently still exists in the deep South, including among some in law enforcement, and the hypocrisy with which people try to hide but not deal with or change their feelings.<br /><br />Iles has at least two instances of unexpected help coming from unexpected places, a device that often gets to me. <div id="review_2802043454" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2802043454" />
    <a title="Jonathan K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32433113-jonathan-k"><img alt="Jonathan K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404758116p2/32433113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2802043454?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonathan K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonathan K" href="/user/show/32433113-jonathan-k">Jonathan K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2802043454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2160233577057889051">I was first introduced to Greg Iles months ago when I stumbled across "Natchez Burning" on the staff picks section at our library. Unfamiliar with the author, I found the pace, plot twists and character depth on par with Pulitzer winners and a momentum factor, similar to a rocket launch. I found Penn Cage, the central character someone I could relate with due to his humanity, selflessness and passion for 'doing the right thing'. Having finished the trilogy, I have been working my way through all</span>
  <span id="freeText2160233577057889051" style="display:none">I was first introduced to Greg Iles months ago when I stumbled across "Natchez Burning" on the staff picks section at our library. Unfamiliar with the author, I found the pace, plot twists and character depth on par with Pulitzer winners and a momentum factor, similar to a rocket launch. I found Penn Cage, the central character someone I could relate with due to his humanity, selflessness and passion for 'doing the right thing'. Having finished the trilogy, I have been working my way through all of Greg's stories and have yet to be disappointed.<br /><br />As a writer, it's always a joy to see a best selling author evolve. This being the first Penn Cage novel, Greg introduces the character's back story, which finds him at a loss having lost his wife to cancer. The 'quiet game' is an analogy to secrets held by people of power who are out of touch with integrity. Those that embody this quality tend to be greedy, narcissistic and fail miserably at what it is to be human. Penn identifies these qualities in the father of a high school lover who he believes is responsible for the murder of a black Natchez citizen, and goes after him with a vengeance. The journey to uncover details of the man's connections to Hoover and others is mind boggling, as is the 'quiet game' he plays with his daughter<br /><br />Personally, I find it difficult NOT to enjoy Greg's storytelling due to how he engages the reader at many levels. For all who want to immerse in the world of Natchez, MS and experience an author of depth and tremendous talent, I urge you to read Greg's books, this one included. He weaves historic elements, science and profound insights into the story fabric which is the true mark of a great author. Enjoy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2160233577057889051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17758251385508375278" style="display:none">Penn Cage is a famous author with his own personal demons, after unsuccessfully trying to move on from the unexpected death of his wife, he takes his young daughter Annie home to Natchez, Mississippi to be with his family. Natchez brings back memories that Penn didn't expect, chief among those is a 30 year old murder motivated by racial tension, politics, and class warfare in 1968. The mystery aspect was interesting, although slightly predictable and not nearly as exciting as all the attempted murder plot points inserted throughout the book. <br /><br />While there was lots of action, and some lovable characters, the book left me wanting more from the story. It dragged on in parts, and could have been cut down significantly. Penn Cage is an engaging character and one I found myself rooting for, however the ending was a little too complex and overly wrought for my liking.</span>

<div id="review_2004584600" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2004584600?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Retired Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Retired Reader" href="/user/show/19481265-retired-reader">Retired Reader</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/23221169-the-quiet-game">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2004584600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2177206042249785908">Absolutely great! I love fiction by Southern authors, and you can almost feel the sultry heat in Greg Isle's words. I was gripped by the story from the first page to the last. Can't wait to read the next in the series. There are so many truths about the South in the pages of this novel, and I am going to make all my friends read it. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_942801732" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/942801732" />
    <a title="Pamela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4894054-pamela"><img alt="Pamela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312308187p2/4894054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/942801732?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pamela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pamela" href="/user/show/4894054-pamela">Pamela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer942801732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6629493213099710905">How I rated this book.<br/><br/>All books start with 5-stars then have stars or partial stars deducted. <br/><br/>1. This book was not jaw-droppingly amazing in the way <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28921.The_Remains_of_the_Day' title='The Remains of the Day by Kazuo Ishiguro' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Remains of the Day</a> or <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37781.Things_Fall_Apart__The_African_Trilogy___1_' title='Things Fall Apart (The African Trilogy, #1) by Chinua Achebe' rel='nofollow noopener'>Things Fall Apart</a> were. Neither was it brilliant, ground-breaking, and thought provoking like pretty much anything by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19916.Jonathan_Coe' title='Jonathan Coe' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jonathan Coe</a> or by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6468.Denis_Johnson' title='Denis Johnson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Denis Johnson</a> is. <br/><br/><i>Deduct one star for non-brilliance. <br/><br/><b>Rating now at 4-stars.</b></i><br/><br/>2. First person. I am not particularly in love with first person. There are times when it works and times when i</span>
  <span id="freeText6629493213099710905" style="display:none">How I rated this book.<br /><br />All books start with 5-stars then have stars or partial stars deducted. <br /><br />1. This book was not jaw-droppingly amazing in the way <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28921.The_Remains_of_the_Day" title="The Remains of the Day by Kazuo Ishiguro" rel="nofollow noopener">The Remains of the Day</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/37781.Things_Fall_Apart__The_African_Trilogy___1_" title="Things Fall Apart (The African Trilogy, #1) by Chinua Achebe" rel="nofollow noopener">Things Fall Apart</a> were. Neither was it brilliant, ground-breaking, and thought provoking like pretty much anything by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19916.Jonathan_Coe" title="Jonathan Coe" rel="nofollow noopener">Jonathan Coe</a> or by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6468.Denis_Johnson" title="Denis Johnson" rel="nofollow noopener">Denis Johnson</a> is. <br /><br /><i>Deduct one star for non-brilliance. <br /><br /><b>Rating now at 4-stars.</b></i><br /><br />2. First person. I am not particularly in love with first person. There are times when it works and times when it doesn't. In this case, it's a draw. <br /><br /><i>Deduct no stars or partial stars for first person, but keep in mind when rounding.</i><br /><br />3. Present tense. I abhor present tense. The only reason for it is in the case of an unreliable narrator as in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5759.Fight_Club" title="Fight Club by Chuck Palahniuk" rel="nofollow noopener">Fight Club</a>. <br /><br /><i>In this case, the present tense became so annoying and so completely unnecessary that I was forced to skim the verbs so that I could pretend it was in past tense. Did this change the tone or impact of the book? Not one bit. <br /><br />Deduct 1/4 star for unnecessary present tense. <br /><br /><b>Rating now at 3.75 stars.</b></i><br /><br />4. Were the characters, the plot, and the action believable? <br /><br /><i>This lawyer is on the scene and involved in several murders, yet never reports them. He is shot at, beat up, threatened, and knocked silly yet he still keeps a tickin'. <br /><br />The characters aren't badly drawn, but they are cliché: The old flame, the new girl friend, the perky little girl, the rich and powerful bad guy. The list goes on and on and on. <br /><br />And the twists! Gracious the twists! I lost count of how many there were. A few twists well done add spice and interest to a crime novel. This many turns it into drudgery. <br /><br />Deduct 1/2 star for unbelievability.<br /><br /><b>Rating now 3.25 stars.</b></i><br /><br />5. How does the book rate with its genre contemporaries?<br /><br /><i>Iles has to compete with the contemporary crime writers such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12470.Michael_Connelly" title="Michael Connelly" rel="nofollow noopener">Michael Connelly</a>(his earlier work), <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8237222.Jo_Nesbo" title="Jo Nesbo" rel="nofollow noopener">Jo Nesbo</a>, etc. He tries, but from the beginning of the book, it's obvious that he is playing way above his league. <br /><br />Deduct 1/4 a star for missing the bar.<br /><br /><b>Rating now at 3 stars.</b> </i><br /><br />6. Did I learn anything about the setting, the main character's occupation, or human behavior from this book.<br /><br /><i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3090113.Paul_Doiron" title="Paul Doiron" rel="nofollow noopener">Paul Doiron</a> has taught me more than I ever wanted to know about what it means to work in the backwoods of Maine.<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4432.Jasper_Fforde" title="Jasper Fforde" rel="nofollow noopener">Jasper Fforde</a> has opened my eyes to the world inside books. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26917.Tony_Hillerman" title="Tony Hillerman" rel="nofollow noopener">Tony Hillerman</a> has taught me about the Navajo people. It is important that writers entertain as well as open your mind to new places, people, thoughts, and experiences. <br /><br />I'm certain that Iles felt he was explaining the culture and people of Mississippi while writing. Unfortunately, he failed and failed miserably. Coming away from the book, I felt that not only did I still not understand modern Mississippi's problems stemming from the Civil Rights Era, I felt that I was being handed a line. When the writer spoke through the main character's thoughts, rather than hearing the explanations and justification that I'm sure the writer intended, I just kept hearing same old tired cop-out: "But don't you see? Some of my best friends are black."<br /><br />Deduct 1/2 star for failing to open a new perspective on an old or unknown topic.<br /><br /><b>Rating now at 2.5 stars.</b></i><br /><br />7. Rounding. Because Goodreads doesn't allow partial star values, and because of the first person irritant, I'm rounding down 1/2 a star.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Final rating: 2 stars</b>
</i> <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6629493213099710905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Esil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3643764-esil"><img alt="Esil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443746908p2/3643764.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/964649984?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Esil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Esil" href="/user/show/3643764-esil">Esil</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer964649984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9837685099134269477">I must admit that I read this book for a strange reason. I read a brilliant review of Natchez Burning, and discovered that it was the 4th in the Penn Cage series. While the review was clear that it's not necessary to read the first three to appreciate Natchez Burning, I am a bit obsessive about reading mystery series in order. A long rationale, but mostly it ended up being worthwhile. I like Penn Cage. I like the setting. I liked the plot. It kept me reading to the end wondering how it would all</span>
  <span id="freeText9837685099134269477" style="display:none">I must admit that I read this book for a strange reason. I read a brilliant review of Natchez Burning, and discovered that it was the 4th in the Penn Cage series. While the review was clear that it's not necessary to read the first three to appreciate Natchez Burning, I am a bit obsessive about reading mystery series in order. A long rationale, but mostly it ended up being worthwhile. I like Penn Cage. I like the setting. I liked the plot. It kept me reading to the end wondering how it would all unfold. But parts of it were a bit trashier than I usually enjoy my mysteries. Also the pacing was a bit crazy and there were long stretches of uninteresting violence. So 3 stars will do it for this one. But the negatives were not enough to turn me off from reading the rest of the series, and in fact I have now started no. 2 in the series, which I am enjoying more. So I might make it to Natchez Burning...</span>

<div id="review_290562362" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/290562362" />
    <a title="Edwin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8061727-edwin"><img alt="Edwin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339605547p2/8061727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/290562362?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edwin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edwin" href="/user/show/8061727-edwin">Edwin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer290562362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16437113611062546644">I only recently discovered Greg Iles (Summer of 2010). The Quiet Game is the second book of his that I have read. Yes, he is a better read than Grisham and his characters are more alive and his description of events closer to home. A little too much violence and murder to be real, but it is a thriller and that is why we are reading him. Iles is particulary adept at bringing the reader into the relationships, and creating the chemistry of Penn Cage and Livy and Penn Cage and Caitlin is nothing sh</span>
  <span id="freeText16437113611062546644" style="display:none">I only recently discovered Greg Iles (Summer of 2010). The Quiet Game is the second book of his that I have read. Yes, he is a better read than Grisham and his characters are more alive and his description of events closer to home. A little too much violence and murder to be real, but it is a thriller and that is why we are reading him. Iles is particulary adept at bringing the reader into the relationships, and creating the chemistry of Penn Cage and Livy and Penn Cage and Caitlin is nothing short of masterful. The sexual content is descriptive and sensual, yet not crass. We have all experienced some of what Iles is telling us when he laments about the past and the present and what we wanted and probably left behind with no hope of ever recovering. As a trial lawyer I am a bit critical of some of the procedural legal gaffs in this book, but they do not detract from the theme or pleasure of reading the book. I don't know anyting about Mississippi legal procedure so I may be wrong anyway. What intrigued me about this book is Iles honest discussion about race. There are so few books, movies, media reports or other dialogue that so honestly deal with the race relations of our country. He calls it as it is, at least from his perspective as a southerner. We should all be so honest. This book is a page turner and I found myself unable to put it down. If you have not read the book, you should.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16437113611062546644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1436892798" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1436892798" />
    <a title="☮Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1076079-karen"><img alt="☮Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605826912p2/1076079.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1436892798?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☮Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="☮Karen" href="/user/show/1076079-karen">☮Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/5710875-the-quiet-game">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1076079-karen?shelf=nook">nook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1076079-karen?shelf=overdrive">overdrive</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1076079-karen?shelf=5000-books">5000-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1076079-karen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1076079-karen?shelf=500-plus-pages">500-plus-pages</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1076079-karen?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1436892798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9202728205549927990"><strong>4.5 stars</strong><br/><br/>Natchez, MS, is from where Penn Cage hails and, following the death of his wife, to where he flees with his little girl. Good memories abound, but danger now, as he looks into a 1968 unsolved murder of a black citizen. His ex, Livy Marston, comes back at the same time, and he wonders if they'll have a second chance at love. She escaped years before, and her father set forth trying to ruin Cage's father for some mysterious reason.<br/><br/><i>Looking up from the bridge, I see Natchez as the tourist s</i></span>
  <span id="freeText9202728205549927990" style="display:none"><strong>4.5 stars</strong><br /><br />Natchez, MS, is from where Penn Cage hails and, following the death of his wife, to where he flees with his little girl. Good memories abound, but danger now, as he looks into a 1968 unsolved murder of a black citizen. His ex, Livy Marston, comes back at the same time, and he wonders if they'll have a second chance at love. She escaped years before, and her father set forth trying to ruin Cage's father for some mysterious reason.<br /><br /><i>Looking up from the bridge, I see Natchez as the tourist sees it: the high bluff where sun-worshiping Natchez Indians massacred the French soldiers of Fort Rosalie in 1729; where Aaron Burr was arrested as a traitor and set free to the cheers of crowds; where an African prince labored twenty years as a slave; where Jefferson Davis wedded Varina Howell in the halcyon days before the Civil War. But I see so much more. I see the city Livy Marston captivated with a beauty and poise not seen since P. T. Barnum brought Jenny Lind down the river in 1851. I see the thin edge of a universe of vibrant life and mysterious death, of shadowy secrets and bright facades, and of races inextricably bound by blood and tears, geography and religion, and above all, time. “This is a good place to be from,” I murmur.</i><br /><br />Natchez is definitely a main character of the book, and I love Iles' descriptions of it, despite the fact that I know I'll probably never set foot there. Other characters are well drawn and interesting. Also present are the ghosts of long-gone folks like Medgar Evans, Martin Luther King, Jr., J Edgar Hoover, and Cage's deceased wife, to name a few.<br />In no time, Penn stirs up the citizenry, who all seem to know who was responsible for the murder but won't talk about it. Even the FBI had been involved, and Hoover sealed the files on the case. All playing "the quiet game." This only makes Cage bolder and more curious to investigate further.<br /><br />There is a bit much going on in this town and in Cage's world to keep up with, and the book being on the longish side became rather exhausting. Answers came slowly, but when they came, wowza! It definitely made me care for Penn Cage and continuing on with another book or two from this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9202728205549927990" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer16757855013597502236">This book had me trapped in the stinging closet of self-loathing for the very short time it took me to race through it.   <span id="freeText16757855013597502236" style="display:none">This book had me trapped in the stinging closet of self-loathing for the very short time it took me to race through it. And thank goodness is was fast-paced, because oh my God did it cause some eyerolling that would have been medically marginal had it continued unabated. The characters were so incredibly stereotypical and alternately condescending/patronizing in so many ways that I audibly sighed to myself while reading this, as if to beg myself to turn back and put this book down. But I couldn't. It was a fun romp and an enjoyable, not too wreckless waste of brain cells. If you like a good murder mystery and don't mind the phrase "poor man's John Grisham" constantly running through your head, pick it up today!</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1753862153" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1753862153" />
    <a title="Purple Country Girl (Sandy)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4150505-purple-country-girl-sandy"><img alt="Purple Country Girl (Sandy)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593213523p2/4150505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1753862153?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Purple Country Girl (Sandy)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Purple Country Girl (Sandy)" href="/user/show/4150505-purple-country-girl-sandy">Purple Country Girl (Sandy)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007545704" href="/book/show/21060937-the-quiet-game">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4150505-purple-country-girl-sandy?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4150505-purple-country-girl-sandy?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4150505-purple-country-girl-sandy?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4150505-purple-country-girl-sandy?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4150505-purple-country-girl-sandy?shelf=legal-supsense">legal-supsense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1753862153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4288009929084142405"><br/>The Quiet Game is slow to get off the ground. It took me almost a month to finish it, after putting it aside several times because the buildup was so, to put it nicely, leisurely. Somewhere around the 100 page mark, it finally picked up and my interest was piqued. It is also very long - my copy, a rather tall paperback, is over 600 pages in length. In all honesty, I think it could have been at least 100 pages shorter and nothing would have been lost. Some of the scenes are very drawn out and the</span>
  <span id="freeText4288009929084142405" style="display:none"><br />The Quiet Game is slow to get off the ground. It took me almost a month to finish it, after putting it aside several times because the buildup was so, to put it nicely, leisurely. Somewhere around the 100 page mark, it finally picked up and my interest was piqued. It is also very long - my copy, a rather tall paperback, is over 600 pages in length. In all honesty, I think it could have been at least 100 pages shorter and nothing would have been lost. Some of the scenes are very drawn out and there are some scenes I don’t think are really necessary to the plot. I don’t like filler in the books I read and I feel there is quite a bit of it here.<br /><br />That said, the story is strong and engaging. Penn Cage, a prosecutor and best-selling author, has returned to his parents’ home in Natchez, Mississippi, following the death of his wife. Penn is still trying to cope as is his young daughter and, with the impending execution of a man he put on death row and the ensuing media circus, it is definitely a good time to lay low with family. What was supposed to be a break for Penn, however, turns into a personal hell as he learns that his father is being blackmailed by a very sketchy character who is also a ex-cop and ex-con.<br /><br />To add further to his troubles, during an interview with Caitlin Masters, an ambitious local journalist, he mentions a decades old cold case that is long-considered to be a racially-motivated murder. A young man, Del Payton, was blown up in his car in 1968, just days after the murder of Martin Luther King, Jr. Payton, a civil rights worker, was a veteran of the Korean War and he was about to be promoted to a new position at the factory where he worked - a position his white colleagues felt was a “white job.” Penn, under the impression that the conversation is off the record, says more than he should and the next morning, after Caitlin has written and printed a story about the unsolved murder quoting Penn, the poop hits the fan and many in the town are angered, leading to violence and threats. <br /><br />To make matters even more complicated, Penn finds Payton’s mother and widow on his parents’ doorstep, pleading with him to find out who murdered Del and to bring the killer to justice. So, instead of finding peace and quiet, Penn finds himself trying to help his father with his blackmailer and also trying to solve a murder that is thirty years old and may involve officials high up in government as well as a man who almost destroyed Penn’s father. The story that follows is full of ups and downs, suspense and lulls, tense scenes full of gunfire and mind-numbing scenes involving Penn and his annoying, selfish ex-girlfriend, Livy. When the suspense is there, it is full on but from time to time, it drags as the more mundane parts of the investigation are pursued and, among other things, as Penn’s relationship with Livy is explored. <br /><br />The Quiet Game is a really good book with some wonderfully-written characters. Watching Penn work to discover the truth is often exciting. So many characters are playing the “quiet game,” basically the last one to talk wins and there are a lot of characters not talking about the Del Payton murder. Iles does an excellent job of describing Natchez past and present. It’s hard to read at times with the racial slurs and the prejudices in both the 60s and 90s. Occasionally, since the book is set in the late 90s, it becomes dated, but not overly so, with the mentions of beepers, camcorders and Sally Jessy Raphael, whose original talk show disappeared in the early 2000s, I believe. <br /><br />While I enjoyed the story, the characters and the twists and turns, the length and slowness did dampen my overall enjoyment. I’m really surprised to see quite a few reviews calling it fast-paced from page one. It was several dozen pages before I would call it fast-paced and even then, there were places were it just idled. I also did not like the use of present tense, I always find this distracting in books. Eventually, I got used to it but I am still not a big fan. <br /><br />Iles is a very good writer and The Quiet Game is an intelligent, complex book but I’m not sure I would read anymore in the Penn Cage series. I glanced at the descriptions and lengths of the next books in the series and I feel they would be more of the same. I won’t say never but definitely not anytime soon. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4288009929084142405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Judy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5778052-judy"><img alt="Judy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493898986p2/5778052.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2225594615?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Judy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Judy" href="/user/show/5778052-judy">Judy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2225594615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4677507353567370699">Two thumbs up to Greg Iles for a stunning legal thriller. I was totally engrossed in this page-turner which is packed with courtroom drama, politics, scandal, secrets and lots of action. I love the character Penn Cage, who is now a best-selling author but earlier was a prosecuting attorney in Texas. Penn and his young daughter have returned to Natchez, Mississippi after the death of his wife in the hopes that his parents can help the 4-year-old get back to some semblance of normalcy. After a sho</span>
  <span id="freeText4677507353567370699" style="display:none">Two thumbs up to Greg Iles for a stunning legal thriller. I was totally engrossed in this page-turner which is packed with courtroom drama, politics, scandal, secrets and lots of action. I love the character Penn Cage, who is now a best-selling author but earlier was a prosecuting attorney in Texas. Penn and his young daughter have returned to Natchez, Mississippi after the death of his wife in the hopes that his parents can help the 4-year-old get back to some semblance of normalcy. After a short time with his parents he finds out his father is being blackmailed. Penn becomes drawn into the investigation of a murder that happened in 1968, 35 years earlier, where a young black man was killed by a car bomb outside the factory where he worked. <br /><br />The writing style reminded me some of John Grisham's early novels. A fun book - I totally enjoyed it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4677507353567370699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3118484399" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer12048513987824468796"> The Quiet Game written by Greg Iles in 1999. It is the first of the Penn Cage series. I have heard from a few other readers how much they enjoy the writing of Greg Ilse's Penn Cage -- Penn is a lawyer who has made the tough conscious decision to do the right thing. The Quiet Game is one of those books, (plus others), sitting on the shelf known as "I will get to you one day". I am so sorry I have waited this long. The Quiet Game is an excellent read which has enough twist and turns to keep the r</span>
  <span id="freeText12048513987824468796" style="display:none"> The Quiet Game written by Greg Iles in 1999. It is the first of the Penn Cage series. I have heard from a few other readers how much they enjoy the writing of Greg Ilse's Penn Cage -- Penn is a lawyer who has made the tough conscious decision to do the right thing. The Quiet Game is one of those books, (plus others), sitting on the shelf known as "I will get to you one day". I am so sorry I have waited this long. The Quiet Game is an excellent read which has enough twist and turns to keep the reader engaged to the end.<br /><br /> "Our actions have consequences that last long after us, entwining the present with the future in ways we cannot begin to understand. I have resolved a simple thing: I will do those things which make me happy today, and which I can live with ten years from now."<br /><br /> </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1011240533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16654850561432644666">A good start to a smart series. Penn Cage is an intelligent writer and semi retired attorney who has a knack for detective work. I liked how his character was introduced and how we were given just enough of a look into his past to let us see why he can be vulnerable at times and ruthless at others. He has a good true nature and never lets on to others just how truly intelligent he is in order to keep them guessing and a little off balance without knowing why. This story has a little something fo</span>
  <span id="freeText16654850561432644666" style="display:none">A good start to a smart series. Penn Cage is an intelligent writer and semi retired attorney who has a knack for detective work. I liked how his character was introduced and how we were given just enough of a look into his past to let us see why he can be vulnerable at times and ruthless at others. He has a good true nature and never lets on to others just how truly intelligent he is in order to keep them guessing and a little off balance without knowing why. This story has a little something for everyone: personal grief, revenge, deception, love, danger, espionage and blindsides. Dick Hill was a great voice for this character and kept a good fast pace without rushing. I hope to listen to more of this series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16654850561432644666" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1343182594" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1343182594" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1343182594?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/25910002-the-quiet-game">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=library-books">library-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=mystery-and-thrillers">mystery-and-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=ebook_kindle">ebook_kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=romance-y">romance-y</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=the_south">the_south</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=politicalish">politicalish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1343182594" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7539306851260167489">So, a couple of years ago, a book called <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18505832.Natchez_Burning__Penn_Cage___4_' title='Natchez Burning (Penn Cage, #4) by Greg Iles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Natchez Burning</a> came out, and it's a pretty doorstop of a thing and I was like "YES. WANT." and then I learned that it was actually the 4th book in a series and then I had the sads. That didn't last long though, because through the magic of my short attention span (or ADD if you believe my previous boss), I forgot all about it until recently. I'm not sure what brought it back to attention, but since it was once again on my radar, I decided to start the se</span>
  <span id="freeText7539306851260167489" style="display:none">So, a couple of years ago, a book called <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18505832.Natchez_Burning__Penn_Cage___4_" title="Natchez Burning (Penn Cage, #4) by Greg Iles" rel="nofollow noopener">Natchez Burning</a> came out, and it's a pretty doorstop of a thing and I was like "YES. WANT." and then I learned that it was actually the 4th book in a series and then I had the sads. That didn't last long though, because through the magic of my short attention span (or ADD if you believe my previous boss), I forgot all about it until recently. I'm not sure what brought it back to attention, but since it was once again on my radar, I decided to start the series... which is THIS book. <br /><br />I managed to lure a couple of friends in with me - 2.0 and Delee. And despite starting this book nearly a week after everyone else, I hammered it out in 2 days. I easily could have and should have finished it in a single day... but see the aforementioned short attention span. I got sucked into Youtube a few times, and then you know, my husband insisted on making sure I was still alive and ambulatory. Rude. <br /><br />Anyway, I really did enjoy this book. Right off the bat, 2.0 and I had a discussion about the narrative style, since it's written in 1st person present narration, which he is not generally a fan of. I rarely notice those things unless they negatively impact the story in some way. But it does usually take a bit of the tension out of the narrative because in order to narrate your story in first person present, you must be alive. Or I guess, you could be a ghost, but that would be a very different type of story. So... Alive, probably. We know that much going in. And knowing that, it means that it's unlikely that our narrative hero will die, so... not as much tension pertaining to the narrator. But that's OK, because there's a lot of things that can happen to a person, or their family, that ratchet it right back up. <br /><br />I don't know if I noticed the narrative style more because of that conversation or not, but I did notice it occasionally. Mostly when it seemed sort of like the narrative was breaking the fourth wall, if that makes sense. But the majority of the time, it was not an issue at all, and I was just absorbed into the story. <br /><br />I will say that the story and the plot worked really well for me. I liked that this, through no intentional act on my part (swear!) fit in perfectly with what I've been reading recently on race relations and such. I probably should have known that a story set in Mississippi would feature race heavily, but I honestly didn't even think about it. I didn't look to see what this was about - I just decided to read it. As I do. <br /><br />I do think that some of the things that happened in this book were... convenient, and probably a mite bit much, but, as a whole, I really liked it, and definitely plan to continue the series. I sort of hope that some of the characters don't make an appearance, or at least as much of an appearance in subsequent books though. <br /><br />One of the major issues that I had with this book (and by major, I mean, slight annoyance, because obviously I really enjoyed the whole and this is not anywhere near a dealbreaker, but I'm being nitpicky) was the portrayal of women in the story. It was really... predictable the roles that the women fell into, and the parts that they played. <br />- There was a bit of a love triangle. <br />- There was instant attraction<br />- All featured women were attracted to our main character, unless they are his mother, or his mother figure who were exempt as they were Sanctified Mother characters.<br />- They must all be extraordinarily beautiful. <br />- They must be headstrong, unpredictable and mysterious, passionate, flirtatious, carefree, rebellious, selfish, and did I mention drop-dead, runway-model gorgeous? <br />- All secondary female characters fit into one of two other roles: victim or slut. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I consider Ray's nurse/girlfriend to be the former, for clarity. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />It was... predictable in that way. Thinking about the two main female characters, it would be easy to say "They are both strong, independent women who know what they want and usually get it." But that's untrue. They both leveraged their looks and bodies to attain their goals, neither was relevant in the story except as to how they were relevant to the main character, meaning that they didn't act on their own, but were always directed or acted upon by someone else. Even the report of a sexual assault trauma was viewed from a cold, detached, "use this to score a point" kind of way, and the victim was blamed... and then it was just brushed aside as if it was unimportant. <br /><br />That sexual assault had some huge repercussions, and those repercussions were key to a couple of minor plot points which ended up being convenient to the bigger plot... But the reasoning and the rationale behind the decisions made after the assault just... didn't make sense to me at all. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Essentially, a rich and powerful man's daughter was raped and ended up pregnant. She refused to have an abortion because her father encouraged her to, and she was being stubborn and contrary, despite the fact that she did NOT want the baby, did NOT want any reminders of that night, or the trauma, or anything. She gave the baby up for adoption, which her father handled, and by handled, I mean he sold the baby for a pretty hefty profit. (He's not a nice man.) She finds out that he made a profit off of her pain, and gets pissed at him. Rightly so, but that baby eventually tracked her down after being in the system their whole life, looking for answers about who they are, and she essentially told them to get lost, that she had no interest in them, never did, never will, and they were nothing to her. Which irritates me, because yes, that person exists because of a rape, which is traumatic, but she was NOT forced to bring that baby into the world, and in fact was encouraged to abort, but she chose otherwise. What about the baby's life and pain? What about the child being sold as a fucking commodity? Nah. Unimportant, apparently. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Anyway. I had some issues with that character, and I wouldn't be sorry if they were a one-and-done character in the series, but somehow I doubt it. We will see. <br /><br />Otherwise I did really enjoy the book and the writing, and look forward to reading more. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7539306851260167489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2561473536" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2561473536" />
    <a title="The Cats’ Mother" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5720552-the-cats-mother"><img alt="The Cats’ Mother" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567802395p2/5720552.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2561473536?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Cats’ Mother" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Cats’ Mother" href="/user/show/5720552-the-cats-mother">The Cats’ Mother</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5720552-the-cats-mother?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5720552-the-cats-mother?shelf=from-book-club">from-book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5720552-the-cats-mother?shelf=legal-political-or-spy-thrillers">legal-political-or-spy-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5720552-the-cats-mother?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5720552-the-cats-mother?shelf=continue-this-series">continue-this-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5720552-the-cats-mother?shelf=really-liked">really-liked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5720552-the-cats-mother?shelf=read-more-of-this-author">read-more-of-this-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2561473536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10543309765632161948">This was an outstanding legal/political thriller which has not dated, despite being twenty years old. It’s the first in a series about lawyer turned writer Penn Cage, but is a complete story with a proper ending, which suits me as with so many other series in the go, it may be a while before I get to the next one - although on the strength of this, get to it I will!<br/><br/>Penn Cage (ridiculous name for someone who’s career involved sending people to prison - subconscious literary nominative determinism</span>
  <span id="freeText10543309765632161948" style="display:none">This was an outstanding legal/political thriller which has not dated, despite being twenty years old. It’s the first in a series about lawyer turned writer Penn Cage, but is a complete story with a proper ending, which suits me as with so many other series in the go, it may be a while before I get to the next one - although on the strength of this, get to it I will!<br /><br />Penn Cage (ridiculous name for someone who’s career involved sending people to prison - subconscious literary nominative determinism before it was even a thing? Maybe.) is a former prosecutor turned bestselling author whose wife has died recently, leaving him and their four year old daughter. Returning home to Natchez, Mississippi to heal, he is dragged into a thirty-year old civil rights murder case when his father confessed that he is being blackmailed by a corrupt ex-cop turned felon. With most of the town telling him to drop it due to ongoing racial tensions in the town, Penn faces a choice between doing the right thing, and the safety of his family, but when he discovers that the murder was instigated by the town’s most prominent retired judge, going to court is the only way out - but it could get him killed.<br /><br />I had only read one previous book by Greg Iles, which was quite different in being more of a suspense/domestic thriller. This was like the old John Grisham legal thrillers, but better written and somehow earthier, with a flawed hero and more action. At nearly 600 pages it’s a long book, but from about halfway I tore through it and the suspense holds up all the way through. The only thing I didn’t like was the present tense narration, but it’s still 5 stars from me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10543309765632161948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15770327969802855518">Well, there’s no shortage of plot action in this one. All kinds of crazy events (past & present) come colliding together when Penn Cage moves back home to Natchez, Mississippi with his daughter and agrees to look into an old unsolved murder case.<br/> <br/>Not exactly the relaxing, recuperative trip back home he was expecting. Now, the clock is ticking for him to unravel the twisted hometown history and fight his own demons before they destroy everything that he holds dear. <br/> <br/>Family secrets, conspiracy, gr</span>
  <span id="freeText15770327969802855518" style="display:none">Well, there’s no shortage of plot action in this one. All kinds of crazy events (past &amp; present) come colliding together when Penn Cage moves back home to Natchez, Mississippi with his daughter and agrees to look into an old unsolved murder case.<br /> <br />Not exactly the relaxing, recuperative trip back home he was expecting. Now, the clock is ticking for him to unravel the twisted hometown history and fight his own demons before they destroy everything that he holds dear. <br /> <br />Family secrets, conspiracy, greed, lost love and murder.<br /> <br />Not a short read by any means - There is more than enough action and backstory to fill the pages. I thought it was a bit much at times, however, it came together nicely and I can see where this would lead into an intriguing series.<br /> <br />Overall, very well written with interesting and well-developed characters. A solid 4+ Stars and I am already looking forward to the next one. <br /></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13429015-rhonda?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,
